      <p><b>Uzbekistan</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʊ/: 'u' in 'push'">ʊ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">ʌ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span></span>-,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ʊ/: 'u' in 'push'">ʊ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>: <span lang="uz">Oʻzbekiston</span>, <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Uzbek" title="Help:IPA/Uzbek">[ozbekiˈstɒn]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Uzbekistan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>: <span lang="uz">Oʻzbekiston Respublikasi</span>), is a landlocked <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>. It is surrounded by five countries: <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_border" title="Kazakhstan–Uzbekistan border">north</a>; <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_border" title="Kyrgyzstan–Uzbekistan border">northeast</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_border" title="Tajikistan–Uzbekistan border">southeast</a>; <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_border" title="Afghanistan–Uzbekistan border">south</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> and the autonomous republic of <a href="/wiki/Karakalpakstan" title="Karakalpakstan">Karakalpakstan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_border" title="Turkmenistan–Uzbekistan border">south-west</a>. Along with <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, it is one of two <a href="/wiki/Doubly_landlocked_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Doubly landlocked countries">doubly landlocked countries</a>. </p>
      <p>What is now Uzbekistan was in ancient times part of the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian</a>-speaking region of <a href="/wiki/Transoxiana" title="Transoxiana">Transoxiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turan" title="Turan">Turan</a>. The first recorded settlers were Eastern Iranian nomads, known as <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a>, who founded kingdoms in <a href="/wiki/Khwarazm" title="Khwarazm">Khwarazm</a> (8th–6th centuries BC), <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">Bactria</a> (8th–6th centuries BC), <a href="/wiki/Sogdia" title="Sogdia">Sogdia</a> (8th–6th centuries BC), <a href="/wiki/Fergana_Valley#History" title="Fergana Valley">Fergana</a> (3rd century BC – 6th century AD), and <a href="/wiki/Margiana" title="Margiana">Margiana</a> (3rd century BC – 6th century AD). The area was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranian</a> <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> and, after a period of <a href="/wiki/Greco-Bactrian_Kingdom" title="Greco-Bactrian Kingdom">Macedonian rule</a>, was ruled by the Iranian <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Empire</a> and later by the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>, until the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">Muslim conquest of Persia</a> in the seventh century. The <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">Early Muslim conquests</a> converted most of the people, including the local ruling classes, into adherents of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. During this period, cities such as Samarkand, Khiva, and Bukhara began to grow rich from the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>, and witnessed the emergence of leading figures of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Bukhari" title="Muhammad al-Bukhari">Muhammad al-Bukhari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Tirmidhi" title="Al-Tirmidhi">Al-Tirmidhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ismail_Samani" title="Ismail Samani">Ismail Samani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Biruni" title="Al-Biruni">al-Biruni</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a>. The local <a href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Khwarazmian dynasty">Khwarazmian dynasty</a>, and Central Asia as a whole were decimated by the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_Khwarezmia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol conquest of Khwarezmia">Mongol invasion</a> in the 13th century, after which the region became dominated by Turkic peoples. The city of <a href="/wiki/Shahrisabz" title="Shahrisabz">Shahrisabz</a> was the birthplace of the Turco-Mongol conqueror <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a> (Tamerlane), who in the 14th century established the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a> and was proclaimed the Supreme Emir of <a href="/wiki/Turan" title="Turan">Turan</a> with his capital in <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>, which became a centre of science under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Ulugh_Beg" title="Ulugh Beg">Ulugh Beg</a>, giving birth to the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Renaissance" title="Timurid Renaissance">Timurid Renaissance</a>. The territories of the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_dynasty" title="Timurid dynasty">Timurid dynasty</a> were conquered by <a href="/wiki/Shaybanids" title="Shaybanids">Uzbek Shaybanids</a> in the 16th century, moving the centre of power to <a href="/wiki/Bukhara" title="Bukhara">Bukhara</a>. The region was split into three states: the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">Khanate of Khiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kokand" title="Khanate of Kokand">Khanate of Kokand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Emirate of Bukhara</a>. Conquests by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Babur" title="Babur">Babur</a> towards the east led to the foundation of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>'s newest invasions as <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>. All of Central Asia, <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Central_Asia" title="Russian conquest of Central Asia">was gradually incorporated</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> during the 19th century, with <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a> becoming the political center of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Turkestan" title="Russian Turkestan">Russian Turkestan</a>. In 1924, <a href="/wiki/National_delimitation_in_the_Soviet_Union#National_delimitation_in_Central_Asia" title="National delimitation in the Soviet Union">national delimitation</a> created the <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic">Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic</a> as an independent republic within the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, it declared <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Uzbekistan)" title="Independence Day (Uzbekistan)">independence</a> as the Republic of Uzbekistan on 31 August 1991. </p>
      <p>Uzbekistan has a diverse cultural heritage due to its layers of history and strategic location. Its official language is <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>, a Turkic language written in a <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_alphabet" title="Uzbek alphabet">modified Latin alphabet</a> and spoken natively by approximately 85% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> has widespread use as an inter-ethnic tongue and in governance. <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> constitute 81% of the population, followed by <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> (5.4%), Tajiks (4.0%), Kazakhs (3.0%) and others (6.5%). <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>&nbsp;constitute 79% of the people while 5% follow&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Christianity</a> and 16% of the population follow other religions or are non-religious. A majority of Uzbeks are <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim" title="Non-denominational Muslim">non-denominational Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Uzbekistan is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">SCO</a>. While officially a democratic republic,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> by 2008 <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental</a> <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> organisations defined Uzbekistan as "an authoritarian state with limited civil rights".<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_-_human_rights_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept_-_human_rights-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>, Uzbekistan is a <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a>, constitutional <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. Uzbekistan comprises 12 <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Uzbekistan" title="Regions of Uzbekistan">regions</a> (vilayats), <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent City</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomous</a> republic, <a href="/wiki/Karakalpakstan" title="Karakalpakstan">Karakalpakstan</a>. The capital and largest city of Uzbekistan is <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>. Following the death of <a href="/wiki/Islam_Karimov" title="Islam Karimov">Islam Karimov</a> in 2016, independent Uzbekistan's second president <a href="/wiki/Shavkat_Mirziyoyev" title="Shavkat Mirziyoyev">Shavkat Mirziyoyev</a> started a new course, which was described as a <i>A Quiet Revolution</i> and <i>Revolution from Above</i>. He stated he intended to abolish <a href="/wiki/Cotton_production_in_Uzbekistan#Forced_labour" title="Cotton production in Uzbekistan">cotton slavery</a>, systematic use of child labour,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Exit_visa" class="mw-redirect" title="Exit visa">exit visas</a>, and to introduce a tax reform and create four new <a href="/wiki/Free_economic_zone" title="Free economic zone">free economic zones</a>. He also gave <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">amnesty</a> to some political prisoners. Relations with the neighbouring countries of <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> drastically improved.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Amnesty International 2017/18 report on <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Uzbekistan" title="Human rights in Uzbekistan">human rights in Uzbekistan</a> found remnant repressive measures or lack of universal rule of law, specific issues being a small minority of labour force in cotton fields being forced labour and restrictions on the movement of 'freed' prisoners. A United Nations report of 2020 found much improvement. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Uzbekistan" title="Economy of Uzbekistan">Uzbek economy</a> is in a gradual transition to the <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, with foreign trade policy being based on <a href="/wiki/Import_substitution_industrialization" title="Import substitution industrialization">import substitution</a>. In September 2017, the country's currency became fully convertible at market rates. Uzbekistan is a major producer and exporter of <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>. With the gigantic power-generation facilities from the Soviet era and an ample supply of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>, Uzbekistan has become the largest electricity producer in Central Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> As of late 2018, the republic was given a BB- rating by both Standard and Poor (S&amp;P) and Fitch. Strengths indicated by <a href="/wiki/Brookings_Institution" title="Brookings Institution">Brookings Institution</a> include Uzbekistan having large liquid assets, high economic growth, and low public debt. Among the constraints holding the republic back are low GDP per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
