      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name "Uzbegistán" appears in the 16th century <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Muhammad_Haidar_Dughlat" title="Mirza Muhammad Haidar Dughlat">Tarikh-i Rashidi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Three roots vie as to the adjective accompanying <i><a href="/wiki/-stan" title="-stan">-stan</a></i> (in the family of <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian languages</a>: "land of"): </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>"free", "independent" or the "lord himself" requiring an <a href="/wiki/Amalgamation_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amalgamation (linguistics)">amalgamation</a> of <i>uz</i> (<a href="/wiki/Turkic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkic language">Turkic</a>: "own"), <i>bek</i> ("master" or "leader")<sup id="cite_ref-H._Keane,_A._Hingston_Quiggin_p.312_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H._Keane,_A._Hingston_Quiggin_p.312-26">[26]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Eponym" title="Eponym">eponymously</a> named after <a href="/wiki/Oghuz_Khagan" title="Oghuz Khagan">Oghuz Khagan</a>, also known as <i>Oghuz Beg</i><sup id="cite_ref-H._Keane,_A._Hingston_Quiggin_p.312_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H._Keane,_A._Hingston_Quiggin_p.312-26">[26]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>A contraction of <i>Uğuz</i>, earlier Oğuz, that is, <a href="/wiki/Oghuz_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oghuz (tribe)">Oghuz (tribe)</a>, amalgamated with <i>bek</i> "<a href="/wiki/Oghuz_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oghuz (tribe)">oguz</a>-leader".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
      </ol> 
      <p>All three have the middle syllable/phoneme being <a href="/wiki/Cognate_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cognate (linguistics)">cognate</a> with Turkic title <i><a href="/wiki/Beg_(title)" class="mw-redirect" title="Beg (title)">Beg</a></i>. </p>
      <p>The place was often spelled as “Ўзбекистон” in Cyrillic, the script used during Soviet rule. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Uzbekistan" title="History of Uzbekistan">History of Uzbekistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg/220px-Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg/330px-Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg/440px-Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1170" data-file-height="1300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kaunakes_Bactria_Louvre_AO31917.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Female statuette wearing the <a href="/wiki/Kaunakes" title="Kaunakes">kaunakes</a>. Chlorite and limestone, <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">Bactria</a>, beginning of the 2nd millennium BC.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_and_Bucephalus_-_Battle_of_Issus_mosaic_-_Museo_Archeologico_Nazionale_-_Naples_BW.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Alexander_and_Bucephalus_-_Battle_of_Issus_mosaic_-_Museo_Archeologico_Nazionale_-_Naples_BW.jpg/220px-Alexander_and_Bucephalus_-_Battle_of_Issus_mosaic_-_Museo_Archeologico_Nazionale_-_Naples_BW.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Alexander_and_Bucephalus_-_Battle_of_Issus_mosaic_-_Museo_Archeologico_Nazionale_-_Naples_BW.jpg/330px-Alexander_and_Bucephalus_-_Battle_of_Issus_mosaic_-_Museo_Archeologico_Nazionale_-_Naples_BW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Alexander_and_Bucephalus_-_Battle_of_Issus_mosaic_-_Museo_Archeologico_Nazionale_-_Naples_BW.jpg/440px-Alexander_and_Bucephalus_-_Battle_of_Issus_mosaic_-_Museo_Archeologico_Nazionale_-_Naples_BW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3905" data-file-height="2766"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Napoli_BW_2013-05-16_16-24-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Issus" title="Battle of Issus">Battle of Issus</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">Mosaic</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Naples_National_Archaeological_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Naples National Archaeological Museum">National Archaeological Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples,_Italy" class="mw-redirect" title="Naples, Italy">Naples</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first people known to have inhabited Central Asia were <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> who came from the northern grasslands of what is now Uzbekistan, sometime in the first millennium BC; when these nomads settled in the region they built an extensive irrigation system along the rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-earlyhistory_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-earlyhistory-28">[28]</a></sup> At this time, cities such as Bukhoro (<a href="/wiki/Bukhara" title="Bukhara">Bukhara</a>) and Samarqand (<a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>) emerged as centres of government and high culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-earlyhistory_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-earlyhistory-28">[28]</a></sup> By the fifth century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">Bactrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soghdia" class="mw-redirect" title="Soghdia">Soghdian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yuezhi" title="Yuezhi">Tokharian</a> states dominated the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-earlyhistory_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-earlyhistory-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As East Asian countries began to develop its silk trade with the West, Persian cities took advantage of this commerce by becoming centres of trade. Using an extensive network of cities and rural settlements in the province of <a href="/wiki/Transoxiana" title="Transoxiana">Transoxiana</a>, and further east in what is today China's <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> Uygur Autonomous Region, the Sogdian intermediaries became the wealthiest of these Iranian merchants. As a result of this trade on what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Route" class="mw-redirect" title="Silk Route">Silk Route</a>, Bukhara and Samarkand eventually became extremely wealthy cities, and at times <a href="/wiki/Transoxiana" title="Transoxiana">Transoxiana</a> (Mawarannahr) was one of the most influential and powerful Persian provinces of antiquity.<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-earlyhistory_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-earlyhistory-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG/220px-1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG/330px-1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG/440px-1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3144" data-file-height="2344"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1872_Vereshchagin_Triumphierend_anagoria.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Triumphant crowd at <a href="/wiki/Registan" title="Registan">Registan</a>, Sher-Dor Madrasah. The <a href="/wiki/Emir_of_Bukhara" class="mw-redirect" title="Emir of Bukhara">Emir of Bukhara</a> viewing the <a href="/wiki/Decapitation" title="Decapitation">severed heads</a> of Russian soldiers on poles. Painting by <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Vereshchagin" title="Vasily Vereshchagin">Vasily Vereshchagin</a> (1872).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karazin_-_Entry_of_Russian_troops_into_Samarkand_1868.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Karazin_-_Entry_of_Russian_troops_into_Samarkand_1868.jpg/220px-Karazin_-_Entry_of_Russian_troops_into_Samarkand_1868.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Karazin_-_Entry_of_Russian_troops_into_Samarkand_1868.jpg/330px-Karazin_-_Entry_of_Russian_troops_into_Samarkand_1868.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Karazin_-_Entry_of_Russian_troops_into_Samarkand_1868.jpg/440px-Karazin_-_Entry_of_Russian_troops_into_Samarkand_1868.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2529" data-file-height="1389"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KarazinNN_VstRusVoyskGRM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russian troops taking <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a> in 1868, by <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Karazin" title="Nikolay Karazin">Nikolay Karazin</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 327 BC Macedonian ruler <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> conquered the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persian Empire</a> provinces of Sogdiana and Bactria, which contained the territories of modern Uzbekistan. A conquest was supposedly of little help to Alexander as popular resistance was fierce, causing Alexander's army to be bogged down in the region that became the northern part of the Macedonian <a href="/wiki/Greco-Bactrian_Kingdom" title="Greco-Bactrian Kingdom">Greco-Bactrian Kingdom</a>. The kingdom was replaced with the Yuezhi dominated <a href="/wiki/Kushan_Empire" title="Kushan Empire">Kushan Empire</a> in the 1st century BC. For many centuries the region of Uzbekistan was ruled by the Persian empires, including the <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sassanid" class="mw-redirect" title="Sassanid">Sassanid</a> Empires, as well as by other empires, for example, those formed by the Turko-Persian <a href="/wiki/Hephthalite" class="mw-redirect" title="Hephthalite">Hephthalite</a> and Turkic <a href="/wiki/Gokturk" class="mw-redirect" title="Gokturk">Gokturk</a> peoples. </p>
      <p>In the 8th century, Transoxiana, the territory between the <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amudarya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syr_Darya" title="Syr Darya">Syrdarya</a> rivers, was conquered by the Arabs (Ali ibn Sattor) becoming a focal point soon after of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>. Many notable scientists lived there and contributed to its development after the conquest. Among the achievements of the scholars during this period were the development of <a href="/wiki/Trigonometry" title="Trigonometry">trigonometry</a> into its modern form (simplifying its practical application to calculate the phases of the moon), advances in <a href="/wiki/Optics" title="Optics">optics</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>, as well as in poetry, philosophy, art, calligraphy, and many others, which set the foundation for the Muslim Renaissance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In the 9th and 10th centuries, Transoxiana was included into the <a href="/wiki/Samanid" class="mw-redirect" title="Samanid">Samanid</a> State. Later, Transoxiana saw the incursion of the Turkic-ruled <a href="/wiki/Karakhanids" class="mw-redirect" title="Karakhanids">Karakhanids</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Seljuks" class="mw-redirect" title="Seljuks">Seljuks</a> (Sultan Sanjar) and <a href="/wiki/Kara-Khitans" class="mw-redirect" title="Kara-Khitans">Kara-Khitans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol</a> conquest under <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a> during the 13th century would bring about a change to the region. The <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Central_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol invasion of Central Asia">Mongol invasion of Central Asia</a> led to the displacement of some of the Iranian-speaking people of the region, their culture and heritage being superseded by that of the <a href="/wiki/Mongols" title="Mongols">Mongolian</a>-<a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a> who came thereafter. The invasions of Bukhara, Samarkand, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ne%C3%BCrgen%C3%A7" class="mw-redirect" title="Köneürgenç">Urgench</a> and others resulted in <a href="/wiki/Destruction_under_the_Mongol_Empire" title="Destruction under the Mongol Empire">mass murders</a> and unprecedented destruction, such as portions of <a href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_Empire" title="Khwarazmian Empire">Khwarezmia</a> being completely razed.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the death of Genghis Khan in 1227, his empire was divided among his four sons and his family members. Despite the potential for serious fragmentation, the Mongol law of the Mongol Empire maintained orderly succession for several more generations, and control of most of Transoxiana stayed in the hands of the direct descendants of <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khan" title="Chagatai Khan">Chagatai Khan</a>, the second son of Genghis Khan. Orderly succession, prosperity, and internal peace prevailed in the Chaghatai lands, and the Mongol Empire as a whole remained a strong and united kingdom (Ulus Batiy, Sattarkhan).<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-Timur_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-Timur-31">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sartscrop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Sartscrop.jpg/190px-Sartscrop.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Sartscrop.jpg/285px-Sartscrop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Sartscrop.jpg/380px-Sartscrop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2731" data-file-height="2351"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sartscrop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Two <a href="/wiki/Sart" title="Sart">Sart</a> men and two Sart boys in <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>, c. 1910
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During this period, most of present Uzbekistan was part of the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a> except <a href="/wiki/Khwarezm" class="mw-redirect" title="Khwarezm">Khwarezm</a> was part of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>. After the decline of the Golden Horde, Khwarezm was briefly ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Sufi_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi Dynasty">Sufi Dynasty</a> till Timur's conquest of it in 1388.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Sufids rules Khwarezm as vassals of alternatively <a href="/wiki/Timurids" class="mw-redirect" title="Timurids">Timurids</a>, Golden Horde and <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Bukhara" title="Khanate of Bukhara">Uzbek Khanate</a> till Persian occupation in 1510. </p>
      <p>In the early 14th century, however, as the empire began to break up into its constituent parts, the Chaghatai territory was disrupted as the princes of various tribal groups competed for influence. One tribal chieftain, <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a> (Tamerlane),<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> emerged from these struggles in the 1380s as the dominant force in Transoxiana. Although, he was not a descendant of Genghis Khan, Timur became the <i>de facto</i> ruler of Transoxiana and proceeded to conquer all of western Central Asia, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia Minor">Asia Minor</a>, and the southern steppe region north of the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>. He also invaded <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> before dying during an invasion of <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">China</a> in 1405.<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-Timur_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-Timur-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Timur was known for his extreme brutality and his conquests were accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Genocidal_massacre" title="Genocidal massacre">genocidal massacres</a> in the cities he occupied.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Timur initiated the last flowering of Transoxiana by gathering together numerous artisans and scholars from the vast lands he had conquered into his capital, Samarqand. By supporting such people, he imbued his empire with a rich Perso-Islamic culture. During his reign and the reigns of his immediate descendants, a wide range of religious and palatial construction masterpieces were undertaken in Samarqand and other population centres.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Amir Timur initiated an exchange of medical discoveries and patronised physicians, scientists and artists from the neighbouring regions such as India;<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> His grandson <a href="/wiki/Ulugh_Beg" title="Ulugh Beg">Ulugh Beg</a> was one of the world's first great astronomers. It was during the Timurid dynasty that Turkic, in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_language" title="Chagatai language">Chaghatai</a> dialect, became a literary language in its own right in Transoxiana, although the Timurids were Persianate in nature. The greatest Chaghataid writer, <a href="/wiki/Ali-Shir_Nava%27i" title="Ali-Shir Nava'i">Ali-Shir Nava'i</a>, was active in the city of <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a> (now in northwestern Afghanistan) in the second half of the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-Timur_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-Timur-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Timurid state quickly split in half after the death of Timur. The chronic internal fighting of the Timurids attracted the attention of the Uzbek nomadic tribes living to the north of the Aral Sea. In 1501 the Uzbek forces began a wholesale invasion of Transoxiana.<sup id="cite_ref-Lubin-Timur_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lubin-Timur-31">[31]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Slave_trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Khanate of Bukhara</a> became prominent and was firmly established.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Before the arrival of the Russians, present Uzbekistan was divided between <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Emirate of Bukhara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khanate" title="Khanate">khanates</a> of <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">Khiva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kokand" title="Khanate of Kokand">Kokand</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> began to expand and spread into <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>. There were 210,306 Russians living in Uzbekistan in 1912.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The "<a href="/wiki/Great_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Game">Great Game</a>" period is generally regarded as running from approximately 1813 to the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Convention_of_1907" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Russian Convention of 1907">Anglo-Russian Convention of 1907</a>. A second, less intensive phase followed the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">Bolshevik Revolution</a> of 1917. At the start of the 19th century, there were some 3,200 kilometres (2,000&nbsp;mi) separating <a href="/wiki/British_India" class="mw-redirect" title="British India">British India</a> and the outlying regions of <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Russia">Tsarist Russia</a>. Much of the land between was unmapped. </p>
      <p>By the beginning of 1920, Central Asia was firmly in the hands of Russia and, despite some early resistance to the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a>, Uzbekistan and the rest of Central Asia became a part of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. On 27 October 1924 the <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic">Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was created. From 1941 to 1945, during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, 1,433,230 people from Uzbekistan fought in the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> against <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>. A number also <a href="/wiki/Ostlegionen" title="Ostlegionen">fought on the German side</a>. As many as 263,005 Uzbek soldiers died in the battlefields of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>, and 32,670 went missing in action.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 20 June 1990, Uzbekistan declared its state sovereignty. On 31 August 1991, Uzbekistan declared independence after the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">failed coup attempt</a> in Moscow. 1 September was proclaimed the National Independence Day. The Soviet Union was <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolved</a> on 26 December of that year. </p>
      <p>President <a href="/wiki/Islam_Karimov" title="Islam Karimov">Islam Karimov</a>, the authoritative ruler of Uzbekistan since independence, died on 2 September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> He was replaced by his long-time <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Uzbekistan" title="Prime Minister of Uzbekistan">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shavkat_Mirziyoyev" title="Shavkat Mirziyoyev">Shavkat Mirziyoyev</a>, on 14 December of the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Uzbekistan" title="Geography of Uzbekistan">Geography of Uzbekistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Uzbekistan" title="List of cities in Uzbekistan">List of cities in Uzbekistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UN-Uzbekistan.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/UN-Uzbekistan.svg/250px-UN-Uzbekistan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/UN-Uzbekistan.svg/375px-UN-Uzbekistan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/UN-Uzbekistan.svg/500px-UN-Uzbekistan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="753" data-file-height="559"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UN-Uzbekistan.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Uzbekistan, including the former <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Uzbekistan has an area of 447,400 square kilometres (172,700&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is the 56th largest country in the world by area and the 42nd by population.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Among the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> countries, it is the 4th largest by area and the 2nd largest by population.<sup id="cite_ref-uzstat_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uzstat-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Uzbekistan lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">37°</a> and <a href="/wiki/46th_parallel_north" title="46th parallel north">46° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/56th_meridian_east" title="56th meridian east">56°</a> and <a href="/wiki/74th_meridian_east" title="74th meridian east">74° E</a>. It stretches 1,425 kilometres (885&nbsp;mi) from west to east and 930 kilometres (580&nbsp;mi) from north to south. Bordering <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Aralkum_Desert" title="Aralkum Desert">Aralkum Desert</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>) to the north and northwest, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> to the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> to the southeast, and <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> to the northeast, Uzbekistan is one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asian</a> states and the only Central Asian state to border all the other four. Uzbekistan also shares a short border (less than 150&nbsp;km or 93&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> to the south. </p>
      <p>Uzbekistan is a dry, <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>. It is one of two <a href="/wiki/Doubly_landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Doubly landlocked">doubly landlocked</a> countries in the world (that is, a landlocked country completely surrounded by other landlocked countries), the other being <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>. In addition, due to its location within a series of <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">endorheic basins</a>, none of its rivers lead to the sea. Less than 10% of its territory is intensively cultivated irrigated land in river valleys and oases, and formerly in the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>, which has largely desiccated in one of the world's worst environmental disasters.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The rest is the vast <a href="/wiki/Kyzylkum_Desert" title="Kyzylkum Desert">Kyzylkum Desert</a> and mountains. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1786" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_UZB_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Uzbekistan map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The highest point in Uzbekistan is <a href="/wiki/Khazret_Sultan" title="Khazret Sultan">Khazret Sultan</a> at 4,643 metres (15,233&nbsp;ft) above sea level, in the southern part of the <a href="/wiki/Gissar_Range" title="Gissar Range">Gissar Range</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Surxondaryo_Region" title="Surxondaryo Region">Surxondaryo Region</a> on the border with Tajikistan, just northwest of <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe" title="Dushanbe">Dushanbe</a> (formerly called Peak of the 22nd Congress of the Communist Party).<sup id="cite_ref-uzstat_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uzstat-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The climate in Uzbekistan is continental, with little <a href="/wiki/Precipitation" title="Precipitation">precipitation</a> expected annually (100–200 millimetres, or 3.9–7.9&nbsp;inches). The average summer high <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a> tends to be 40&nbsp;°C <span class="nowrap">(104 °F)</span>, while the average winter low temperature is around −23&nbsp;°C <span class="nowrap">(−9 °F)</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-LoC:Climate_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC:Climate-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Uzbekistan is home to six terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Alai-Western_Tian_Shan_steppe" class="mw-redirect" title="Alai-Western Tian Shan steppe">Alai-Western Tian Shan steppe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gissaro-Alai_open_woodlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Gissaro-Alai open woodlands">Gissaro-Alai open woodlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badghyz_and_Karabil_semi-desert" title="Badghyz and Karabil semi-desert">Badghyz and Karabil semi-desert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_northern_desert" title="Central Asian northern desert">Central Asian northern desert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_riparian_woodlands" title="Central Asian riparian woodlands">Central Asian riparian woodlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_southern_desert" title="Central Asian southern desert">Central Asian southern desert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg/220px-Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg/330px-Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg/440px-Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="3194"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karakalpakstan_Kyzyl_Qala_Cotton_Picking.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cotton picking near <a href="/wiki/Kyzyl-Kala" title="Kyzyl-Kala">Kyzyl-Kala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karakalpakstan" title="Karakalpakstan">Karakalpakstan</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Uzbekistan has a rich and diverse natural environment. However, decades of questionable <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> policies in pursuit of greater <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> production have resulted in a catastrophic scenario with the agricultural industry being the main contributor to the pollution and devastation of both air and water in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a> used to be the fourth-largest inland sea on Earth, acting as an influencing factor in the air moisture and arid land use.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Since the 1960s, the decade when the overuse of the Aral Sea water began, it has shrunk to about 10% of its former area and divided into parts, with only the southern part of the narrow western lobe of the <a href="/wiki/South_Aral_Sea" title="South Aral Sea">South Aral Sea</a> remaining permanently in Uzbekistan. Reliable, or even approximate data, have not been collected, stored, or provided by any organisation or official agency.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Much of the water was and continues to be used for the <a href="/wiki/Cotton_production_in_Uzbekistan" title="Cotton production in Uzbekistan">irrigation of cotton fields</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-49">[49]</a></sup> a crop requiring a large amount of water to grow.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to the Aral Sea problem, high salinity and contamination of the soil with <a href="/wiki/Heavy_elements" class="mw-redirect" title="Heavy elements">heavy elements</a> are especially widespread in <a href="/wiki/Karakalpakstan" title="Karakalpakstan">Karakalpakstan</a>, the region of Uzbekistan adjacent to the Aral Sea. The bulk of the nation's water resources is used for farming, which accounts for nearly 84% of the water usage and contributes to high <a href="/wiki/Soil_salinity" title="Soil salinity">soil salinity</a>. Heavy use of <a href="/wiki/Pesticide" title="Pesticide">pesticides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fertiliser" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertiliser">fertilisers</a> for cotton growing further aggravates <a href="/wiki/Soil_contamination" title="Soil contamination">soil contamination</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LoC:Climate_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LoC:Climate-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Suv-ombori.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Suv-ombori.gif/220px-Suv-ombori.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Suv-ombori.gif/330px-Suv-ombori.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Suv-ombori.gif/440px-Suv-ombori.gif 2x" data-file-width="2363" data-file-height="1396"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Suv-ombori.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of flooded areas as a result of the collapse of the Sardoba Reservoir
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the UNDP (United Nations Development Program), <a href="/wiki/Climate_risk" title="Climate risk">climate risk</a> management in Uzbekistan needs to consider its ecological safety.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AralSea1989_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/AralSea1989_2014.jpg/220px-AralSea1989_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/AralSea1989_2014.jpg/330px-AralSea1989_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/AralSea1989_2014.jpg/440px-AralSea1989_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="870"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AralSea1989_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Comparison of the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a> between 1989 and 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Numerous oil and gas deposits have been discovered in the south of the country. </p>
      <p>Uzbekistan has also been home to seismic activity, as evidenced by the <a href="/wiki/1902_Andijan_earthquake" title="1902 Andijan earthquake">1902 Andijan earthquake</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_Fergana_Valley_earthquake" title="2011 Fergana Valley earthquake">2011 Fergana Valley earthquake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1966_Tashkent_earthquake" title="1966 Tashkent earthquake">1966 Tashkent earthquake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A dam collapse at Sardoba reservoir in May 2020 flooded a lot of farmland and villages; the devastation extended into areas inside neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Uzbekistan" title="Politics of Uzbekistan">Politics of Uzbekistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Oliy_Majlis_(Parliament_of_Uzbekistan).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Oliy_Majlis_%28Parliament_of_Uzbekistan%29.jpg/220px-Oliy_Majlis_%28Parliament_of_Uzbekistan%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Oliy_Majlis_%28Parliament_of_Uzbekistan%29.jpg/330px-Oliy_Majlis_%28Parliament_of_Uzbekistan%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Oliy_Majlis_%28Parliament_of_Uzbekistan%29.jpg/440px-Oliy_Majlis_%28Parliament_of_Uzbekistan%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1227" data-file-height="818"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Oliy_Majlis_(Parliament_of_Uzbekistan).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Chamber_of_Uzbekistan" title="Legislative Chamber of Uzbekistan">Legislative Chamber of the Supreme Assembly</a> (Lower House).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Islam_Karimov_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Islam_Karimov_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Islam_Karimov_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Islam_Karimov_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Islam_Karimov_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Islam_Karimov_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Islam_Karimov_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="912" data-file-height="1216"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Islam_karimov_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Islam_Karimov" title="Islam Karimov">Islam Karimov</a>, the first President of Uzbekistan, during a visit to the Pentagon in 2002
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg/220px-Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg/330px-Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg/440px-Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1028" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Shavkat_Mirziyoyev_official_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Shavkat_Mirziyoyev" title="Shavkat Mirziyoyev">Shavkat Mirziyoyev</a>, the current President of Uzbekistan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After Uzbekistan declared independence from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in 1991, an election was held, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_Karimov" title="Islam Karimov">Islam Karimov</a> was elected as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Uzbekistan" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Uzbekistan">first President</a> of Uzbekistan on 29 December 1991. </p>
      <p>The elections of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Assembly_(Uzbekistan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Assembly (Uzbekistan)">Oliy Majlis</a> (Parliament or Supreme Assembly) were held under a resolution adopted by the 16th Supreme Soviet in 1994. In that year, the Supreme Soviet was replaced by the Oliy Majlis. </p>
      <p>The third elections for the bicameral 150-member Oliy Majlis, the Legislative Chamber, and the 100-member Senate for five-year terms, were held on 27 December 2009. The second elections were held from December 2004 to January 2005. The Oliy Majlis was unicameral up to 2004. Its size increased from 69 deputies (members) in 1994 to 120 in 2004–05 and currently stands at 150. </p> 
      <table class="box-Confusing plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-confusing" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48">
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>may be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness">confusing or unclear</a> to readers</b>. In particular, the last paragraph seems to lack preceding context.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">clarify the section</a>. There might be a discussion about this on <a href="/wiki/Talk:Uzbekistan" title="Talk:Uzbekistan">the talk page</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Karimov's first presidential term was extended to 2000 via a <a href="/wiki/1995_Uzbek_presidential_term_referendum" title="1995 Uzbek presidential term referendum">referendum</a>, and he was re-elected in <a href="/wiki/2000_Uzbekistani_presidential_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2000 Uzbekistani presidential election">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Uzbekistani_presidential_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Uzbekistani presidential election">2007</a>, and 2015, each time receiving over 90% of the vote. Most international observers refused to participate in the process and did not recognise the results, dismissing them as not meeting basic standards. </p>
      <p>The 2002 referendum also included a plan for a bicameral parliament consisting of a lower house (the Oliy Majlis) and an upper house (Senate). Members of the lower house are to be "full-time" legislators. Elections for the new bicameral parliament took place on 26 December. </p>
      <p>Following Islam Karimov's death on 2 September 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Assembly_(Uzbekistan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Assembly (Uzbekistan)">Supreme Assembly</a> appointed Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Shavkat_Mirziyoyev" title="Shavkat Mirziyoyev">Shavkat Mirziyoyev</a> as interim president. Although the chairman of the Senate, <a href="/wiki/Nigmatilla_Yuldashev" title="Nigmatilla Yuldashev">Nigmatilla Yuldashev</a>, was constitutionally designated as Karimov's successor, Yuldashev proposed that Mirziyoyev take the post of the interim president instead in light of Mirziyoyev's "many years of experience". Mirziyoyev was subsequently elected as the country's second president in the <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistani_presidential_election,_2016" class="mw-redirect" title="Uzbekistani presidential election, 2016">December 2016 presidential election</a>, winning 88.6% of the vote, and was sworn in on 14 December. Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Abdulla_Aripov" title="Abdulla Aripov">Abdulla Aripov</a> replaced him as prime minister. </p>
      <p>Mirziyoyev removed most of Karimov's officials and urged the government to employ "new, young people who love their country." After a year in office, Mirziyoyev moved away from many of his predecessor's policies. He visited all the Uzbek regions and big cities to get acquainted with the implementation of the projects and reforms which he ordered. Many analysts and Western media compared his rule with <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Deng_Xiaoping" title="Deng Xiaoping">Deng Xiaoping</a> or <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Communist Party">Soviet Communist Party</a> general secretary <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>. His rule has been quoted as being an "Uzbek Spring".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mirziyoyev was nominated as a candidate for the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> by Olimzhon Tukhtanazarov, who is a representative of the ruling <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan_Liberal_Democratic_Party" title="Uzbekistan Liberal Democratic Party">Liberal Democratic Party</a> in 2018. He was not short-listed and did not win. By the end of that year, he had been named the "Asian of the Year of 2018" by the Asia Journalist Association (AJA).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Uzbekistan" title="Foreign relations of Uzbekistan">Foreign relations of Uzbekistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_organization_membership_of_Uzbekistan" title="International organization membership of Uzbekistan">International organization membership of Uzbekistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg/220px-Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg/330px-Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg/440px-Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1892" data-file-height="1292"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Baku_hosts_7th_Summit_of_Cooperation_Council_of_Turkic-Speaking_States_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Representatives of Uzbekistan at the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_Council" title="Turkic Council">Turkic Council</a> meeting in <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Uzbekistan joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> in December 1991. However, it is opposed to reintegration and withdrew from the CIS collective security arrangement in 1999. Since that time, Uzbekistan has participated in the CIS peacekeeping force in Tajikistan and in UN-organized groups to help resolve the Tajikistan and Afghanistan conflicts, both of which it sees as posing threats to its own stability. </p>
      <p>Previously close to Washington (which gave Uzbekistan half a billion dollars in aid in 2004, about a quarter of its military budget), the government of Uzbekistan has recently restricted American military use of the airbase at <a href="/wiki/Karshi-Khanabad" class="mw-redirect" title="Karshi-Khanabad">Karshi-Khanabad</a> for air operations in neighbouring Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Uzbekistan was an active supporter of U.S. efforts against worldwide terrorism and joined the coalitions that have dealt with both Afghanistan and Iraq.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The relationship between Uzbekistan and the United States began to deteriorate after the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Colour_revolutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Colour revolutions">colour revolutions</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (and to a lesser extent <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>). When the U.S. joined in a call for an independent international investigation of the bloody events at <a href="/wiki/Andijan_massacre" title="Andijan massacre">Andijan</a>, the relationship further declined, and President Islam Karimov changed the political alignment of the country to bring it closer to Russia and China. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_(22052330394).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_%2822052330394%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_%2822052330394%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_%2822052330394%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_%2822052330394%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_%2822052330394%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_%2822052330394%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4863" data-file-height="3242"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_President_Karimov_at_the_President%27s_Residential_Compound_in_Samarkand_(22052330394).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Islam_Karimov" title="Islam Karimov">Islam Karimov</a> with U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> in Samarkand in November 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In late July 2005, the government of Uzbekistan ordered the United States to vacate an airbase in Karshi-Kanabad (near Uzbekistan's border with Afghanistan) within 180 days.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-59">[59]</a></sup> Karimov had offered use of the base to the U.S. shortly after <a href="/wiki/9/11" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11">9/11</a>. It is also believed by some Uzbeks that the protests in Andijan were brought about by the UK and U.S. influences in the area of Andijan.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-59">[59]</a></sup> This is another reason for the hostility between Uzbekistan and the West. </p>
      <p>Uzbekistan is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN) (since 2 March 1992), the <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a> (EAPC), <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> (PfP), and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE). It belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC) and the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">Economic Cooperation Organization</a> (ECO) (comprising the five Central Asian countries, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>). In 1999, Uzbekistan joined the <a href="/wiki/GUAM" class="mw-redirect" title="GUAM">GUAM</a> alliance (Georgia, Ukraine, Azerbaijan and <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>), which was formed in 1997 (making it GUUAM), but pulled out of the organisation in 2005. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg/220px-2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg/330px-2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg/440px-2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2015_Summit_of_the_Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Leaders present at the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">SCO</a> summit in <a href="/wiki/Ufa" title="Ufa">Ufa</a>, Russia in 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Uzbekistan is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a> (SCO) and hosts the SCO's Regional Anti-Terrorist Structure (RATS) in Tashkent. Uzbekistan joined the new <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_Cooperation_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Asian Cooperation Organisation">Central Asian Cooperation Organisation</a> (CACO) in 2002. The CACO consists of Uzbekistan, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, and Kyrgyzstan. It is a founding member of, and remains involved in, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_Union" title="Central Asian Union">Central Asian Union</a>, formed with Kazakhstan and Kyrgyzstan, and joined in March 1998 by Tajikistan. </p>
      <p>In September 2006, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> presented Islam Karimov an award for Uzbekistan's preservation of its rich culture and traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Despite criticism, this seems to be a sign of improving relationships between Uzbekistan and the West. </p>
      <p>The month of October 2006 also saw a decrease in the isolation of Uzbekistan from the West. The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> announced that it was planning to send a delegation to Uzbekistan to talk about human rights and liberties, after a long period of hostile relations between the two. Although it is equivocal about whether the official or unofficial version of the <a href="/wiki/Andijan_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Andijan Massacre">Andijan Massacre</a> is true, the EU is evidently willing to ease its economic sanctions against Uzbekistan. Nevertheless, it is generally assumed among Uzbekistan's population that the government will stand firm in maintaining its close ties with the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> and in its theory that the 2004–2005 protests in Uzbekistan were promoted by the US and UK. </p>
      <p>In January 2008, <a href="/wiki/Lola_Karimova-Tillyaeva" title="Lola Karimova-Tillyaeva">Lola Karimova-Tillyaeva</a> was appointed to her current role as Uzbekistan's ambassador to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>. Karimova-Tillyaeva and her team have been instrumental in promoting inter-cultural dialogue by increasing European society's awareness of Uzbekistan's cultural and historical heritage. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Uzbekistan" title="Human rights in Uzbekistan">Human rights in Uzbekistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/2005_Andijan_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 Andijan unrest">2005 Andijan unrest</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Art. 13 of the Constitution of the Republic of Uzbekistan asserts that "Democracy in the Republic of Uzbekistan shall be based upon common human principles, according to which the highest value shall be the human being, his life, freedom, honour, dignity and other inalienable rights."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The official position is summarised in a memorandum "The measures taken by the government of the Republic of Uzbekistan in the field of providing and encouraging human rights"<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and amounts to the following: the government does everything that is in its power to protect and to guarantee the human rights of Uzbekistan's citizens. Uzbekistan continuously improves its laws and institutions in order to create a more humane society. Over 300 laws regulating the rights and basic freedoms of the people have been passed by the parliament. For instance, an office of <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">Ombudsman</a> was established in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On 2 August 2005, President Islam Karimov signed a decree that abolished capital punishment in Uzbekistan on 1 January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental</a> human rights organisations, such as <a href="/wiki/International_Helsinki_Federation_for_Human_Rights" title="International Helsinki Federation for Human Rights">IHF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>, define Uzbekistan as "an authoritarian state with limited civil rights"<sup id="cite_ref-US_State_Dept_-_human_rights_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_State_Dept_-_human_rights-17">[17]</a></sup> and express profound concern about "wide-scale violation of virtually all basic human rights".<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> According to the reports, the most widespread violations are <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_arrest_and_detention" title="Arbitrary arrest and detention">arbitrary arrests</a>, and various restrictions of freedoms: of religion, of speech and press, of free association and assembly. It has also been reported that forced sterilisation of rural Uzbek women has been sanctioned by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The reports maintain that the violations are most often committed against members of religious organisations, independent journalists, human rights activists and political activists, including members of the banned opposition parties. As of 2015, reports on violations on human rights in Uzbekistan indicated that violations were still going on without any improvement.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> has consistently ranked Uzbekistan near the bottom of its Freedom in the World ranking since the country's founding in 1991. In the 2018 report, Uzbekistan was one of the 11 worst countries for <a href="/wiki/Political_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Political Rights">Political Rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_Liberties" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil Liberties">Civil Liberties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2005_civil_unrest_in_Uzbekistan" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 civil unrest in Uzbekistan">2005 civil unrest in Uzbekistan</a>, which resulted in several hundred people being killed, is viewed by many as a landmark event in the history of human rights abuse in Uzbekistan.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> A concern has been expressed and a request for an independent investigation of the events has been made by the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> the European Union,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> the OSCE Chairman-in-Office and the OSCE Office for Democratic Institutions and Human Rights.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government of Uzbekistan is accused of unlawful termination of human life and of denying its citizens <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly" title="Freedom of assembly">freedom of assembly</a> and freedom of expression. The government vehemently rebuffs the accusations, maintaining that it merely conducted an anti-terrorist operation, exercising only necessary force.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In addition, some officials claim that "an <a href="/wiki/Information_warfare" title="Information warfare">information war</a> on Uzbekistan has been declared" and the human rights violations in Andijan are invented by the enemies of Uzbekistan as a convenient pretext for intervention in the country's internal affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Male <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Uzbekistan" title="LGBT rights in Uzbekistan">homosexuality</a> is illegal in Uzbekistan.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Punishment ranges from a fine to 3 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Uzbekistan also maintains the world's second-highest rate of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_21st_century" title="Slavery in the 21st century">modern slavery</a>, 3.97%<sup id="cite_ref-globalslaveryindex1_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalslaveryindex1-81">[81]</a></sup> of the country's population working as modern slaves. In real terms, this means that there are 1.2 million modern slaves<sup id="cite_ref-globalslaveryindex1_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalslaveryindex1-81">[81]</a></sup> in Uzbekistan. Most work in the cotton industry. The government allegedly forces state employees to pick cotton in the autumn months.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> World Bank loans have been connected to projects that use child labour and forced labour practices in the cotton industry.<sup id="cite_ref-wbloans_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wbloans-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_developments">Recent developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Recent developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Islam Karimov died in 2016 and his successor Shavkat Mirziyoyev is considered by most to be pursuing a less autocratic path by increasing co-operation with human rights NGOs,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> scheduling Soviet-style <a href="/wiki/Travel_visa#Exit_visas" title="Travel visa">exit visas</a> to be abolished in 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and reducing sentences for certain misdemeanor offences.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Amnesty International report on the country for 2017/2018 found some remnant repressive measures and lack of rule of law in eradicating modern slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-88">[88]</a></sup> In February 2020, the United Nations announced that Uzbekistan made "major progress" on stamping out forced labour in its cotton harvest as 94% of pickers worked voluntarily.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Uzbekistan" title="Regions of Uzbekistan">Regions of Uzbekistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Uzbekistan" title="Districts of Uzbekistan">Districts of Uzbekistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Uzbekistan is divided into twelve <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">provinces</a> (<i>viloyatlar</i>, singular <i><a href="/wiki/Viloyat" class="mw-redirect" title="Viloyat">viloyat</a></i>, compound noun <i>viloyati</i> e.g., Toshkent <i>viloyati</i>, Samarqand <i>viloyati</i>, etc.), one <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_republic" title="Autonomous republic">autonomous republic</a> (<i>respublika</i>, compound noun <i>respublikasi</i> e.g. Qoraqalpogʻiston Muxtor <i>Respublikasi</i>, Karakalpakstan <i>Autonomous Republic</i>, etc.), and one <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">independent city</a> (<i>shahar</i>, compound noun <i>shahri</i>, e.g., Toshkent <i>shahri</i>). Names are given below in <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Karakalpak_language" title="Karakalpak language">Karakalpak</a> languages when applicable, although numerous variations of the transliterations of each name exist. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Uzbekistan_provinces.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Uzbekistan_provinces.png/350px-Uzbekistan_provinces.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Uzbekistan_provinces.png 1.5x" data-file-width="380" data-file-height="248"></a>

          <a href="/wiki/File:Uzbekistan_provinces.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <p>The provinces are further divided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Uzbekistan" title="Districts of Uzbekistan">districts</a> (<i>tuman</i>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uzbekistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
